# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce artifacts** — Express all code changes as **unified diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT edit source files directly — there are none in your workspace.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# big-code-camel-arch-001: Apache Camel Message Routing Architecture

## Task

Trace how Apache Camel routes a message from endpoint reception through the EIP pipeline to a destination. Map the complete Component→Endpoint→Consumer→Processor→Producer hierarchy, including the Pipeline processor chain, Channel interceptor wiring, and the RouteReifier model-to-runtime bridge.

## Context

- **Repository**: apache/camel (Java, ~2.8M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: core/ — the Camel core routing engine (camel-api, camel-support, camel-core-processor, camel-base-engine, camel-core-reifier)

## Requirements

1. Identify all relevant components in the Component→Endpoint→Consumer→Processor→Producer hierarchy (API interfaces + base implementations)
2. Trace the dependency chain from route definition through reification to runtime message processing
3. Document the Pipeline and Channel architecture (how processors are chained and intercepted)
4. Explain how the RouteReifier bridges the DSL model (RouteDefinition) to the runtime Route

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

72-assistanttext-
I've completed a comprehensive architectural analysis of Apache Camel's message routing system and saved it to `/logs/agent/solution.md`. 

## Summary of Analysis

The analysis maps the complete **Component→Endpoint→Consumer→Processor→Producer** hierarchy through three key architectural patterns:

1. **Reifier Pattern Bridge** — Converts declarative RouteDefinition (DSL model) to runtime Route via RouteReifier and ProcessorReifier classes, transforming 100+ EIP pattern definitions into executable processors

2. **Channel Pattern for Interception** — DefaultChannel wraps each processor in the route graph with:
   - InterceptStrategies (user-defined interceptors)
   - Error handlers (exception management)
   - Debugging/tracing advice (observability)
   - Message history and stream caching (auditing)

3. **Pipeline Pattern for Chaining** — RoutePipeline sequences processors with reactive asynchronous execution, handling exchange copying and conditional routing between each step

The analysis includes:
- **22 key files** identified across the camel-api, camel-base-engine, camel-core-processor, camel-core-reifier, and camel-core-model modules
- **Complete dependency chain** from RouteDefinition through reification to runtime message processing
- **Data flow diagram** showing message reception through consumer/producer to external delivery
- **Interface contracts** defining relationships between components
- **Design patterns** (Factory, Strategy, Adapter, Reifier, Advice) that enable the extensible architecture

methods include `createProducer()`, `createConsumer(Processor)`, `createExchange()`\n- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Producer.java** \u2014 Sends message exchanges to an endpoint; implements Processor interface\n- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Consumer.java** \u2014 Consumes message exchanges from an endpoint; contains `getProcessor()` for message processing\n- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Processor.java** \u2014 Core unit for message processing; single method `process(Exchange exchange)`\n- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Channel.java** \u2014 Intercept channel between processors in route graph; implements the Pipes and Filters pattern (lines 45-150)\n  - `PipelineTask` inner class manages asynchronous processor chaining\n  - `newInstance()` factory method creates pipeline or returns single processor\n- **core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/RoutePipeline.java** \u2014 Specialized Pipeline used as route entry point\n- **core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/DefaultInternalProcessorFactory.java** \u2014 Factory for creating channels and internal processors\n\n### Reifier Layer (camel-core-reifier)\n- **core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/RouteReifier.java** \u2014 Bridge from RouteDefinition (DSL model) to runtime Route\n  - `createRoute()` method (lines 87-98) orchestrates route creation\n  - `doCreateRoute()` method (lines 102-400+) resolves endpoint, creates route, adds processors, and wraps in pipeline\n  - Creates RoutePipeline from event-driven processors (line 263)\n  - Adds InternalProcessor advice for unit of work, route policies, management, and lifecycle\n\n- **core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/ProcessorReifier.java** \u2014 Abstract base for converting processor definitions to runtime Processor instances\n  - `reifier()` static method (lines 184-202) dispatches to appropriate reifier based on definition type\n  - `coreReifier()` method (lines 204-349) maps ProcessorDefinition classes to reifiers (100+ EIP patterns)\n  - `addRoutes()` method (lines 618-637) creates Channel and adds processor to route's event-driven processors\n  - `makeProcessor()` method (lines 834-871) creates processor, injects ID, and wraps in channel\n  - `wrapChannel()` method (lines 654-712) creates Channel, initializes with interceptors, wraps in error handler\n\n### Model Layer (camel-core-model)\n- **core/camel-core-model/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/model/RouteDefinition.java** \u2014 DSL model for route definition (extends OutputDefinition); methods like `from(String uri)` and processor chains\n- **core/camel-core-model/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/model/ProcessorDefinition.java** \u2014 Base class for all EIP processor definitions\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n```\n1. Entry point: RouteDefinition (DSL model in camel-core-model)\n   \u2193\n2. RouteReifier.createRoute() (camel-core-reifier)\n   \u2193\n3. Calls: RouteReifier.doCreateRoute() (lines 102-120)\n   - Resolves Endpoint via Component.createEndpoint()\n   - Creates Route via PluginHelper.getRouteFactory()\n   \u2193\n4. Iterates outputs: ProcessorDefinition \u2192 ProcessorReifier.reifier() (line 231)\n   \u2193\n5. For each output: ProcessorReifier.addRoutes() (lines 618-637)\n   - Calls makeProcessor() to create EIP processor\n   - Wraps in wrapProcessor() \u2192 wrapChannel()\n   \u2193\n6. Creates Channel (line 657)\n   DefaultInternalProcessorFactory.createChannel()\n   \u2193\n7. Initializes Channel: channel.initChannel() (line 698)\n   - Applies InterceptStrategies (lines 662-665)\n   - Wraps with debugger/tracer/history advice (lines 176-227)\n   - Applies InterceptStrategies (lines 231-259)\n   - Wraps in error handler (line 704)\n   \u2193\n8. Route configuration: RouteReifier.doCreateRoute() (lines 253-368)\n   - Collects all event-driven processors\n   - Creates RoutePipeline from processors (line 263)\n   - Wraps in InternalProcessor with UnitOfWork advice\n   - Adds route policies, management, and lifecycle advice\n   \u2193\n9. Runtime: Message flow through Route\n   Endpoint.Consumer \u2192 Pipeline \u2192 Channel (interceptors) \u2192 Processor \u2192 Endpoint.Producer\n```\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n1. **Component\u2192Endpoint\u2192Consumer/Producer Hierarchy**\n   - **Component** (Factory Pattern): Creates Endpoint instances from URIs\n   - **Endpoint** (Strategy Pattern): Represents communication strategy; creates appropriate Consumer/Producer\n   - **Consumer/Producer** (Adapter Pattern): Adapts between external systems and Camel's Processor interface\n   - Each layer is pluggable for different transports (HTTP, JMS, FTP, etc.)\n\n2. **Reifier Pattern (Model-Driven Architecture)**\n   - **RouteDefinition**: DSL model representing route structure (declarative)\n   - **RouteReifier**: Transforms RouteDefinition \u2192 Route (model to runtime)\n   - **ProcessorReifier**: Maps each ProcessorDefinition to concrete Processor implementation\n   - Factory method dispatches on definition class (lines 204-349)\n\n3. **Channel Pattern (Interceptor Wiring)**\n   - **Channel interface**: Wraps each processor in the route graph\n   - **DefaultChannel**: Concrete implementation managing interceptor chains\n   - Interceptors applied in three levels (camelContext, route, processor) sorted by order\n   - Reversed order ensures first interceptor is invoked last (line 234 reversal)\n\n4. **Pipeline Pattern (Processor Chaining)**\n   - **Pipeline**: Chains multiple processors sequentially\n   - **PipelineTask**: Inner class for asynchronous execution using ReactiveExecutor\n   - Each processor's output becomes next processor's input\n   - Handles exchange copying (OUT\u2192IN) between processors\n\n5. **Advice Pattern (Aspect-Oriented)**\n   - **CamelInternalProcessorAdvice**: Applied to channels for cross-cutting concerns\n   - **InternalProcessor**: Wraps route entry with advice chain:\n     - UnitOfWork (transactional boundaries)\n     - RoutePolicy (lifecycle management)\n     - Management (JMX instrumentation)\n     - Lifecycle hooks\n   - **Channel advice** (in DefaultChannel.initChannel):\n     - Debugger/Backlog tracer\n     - Message history\n     - Stream caching\n     - Delayer\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n1. **Component Interface**\n   - Creates Endpoint instances\n   - Handles URI parsing and parameter validation\n   - Manages component-level configuration\n\n2. **Endpoint Interface**\n   - Creates Producer for sending messages\n   - Creates Consumer for receiving messages\n   - Creates Exchange objects for message routing\n   - Manages endpoint-level configuration\n\n3. **Consumer Interface**\n   - Implements event-driven consumption model\n   - Creates Exchange for consumed messages\n   - Invokes Processor for message handling\n   - Manages auto-release of exchanges\n\n4. **Producer Interface**\n   - Extends Processor interface (is-a relationship)\n   - Sends Exchange to endpoint\n   - Handles response exchanges (request-reply)\n\n5. **Processor Interface**\n   - Single responsibility: `process(Exchange exchange)`\n   - Implemented by all EIP patterns (Choice, Multicast, etc.)\n   - Forms basis of entire routing engine\n\n6. **Channel Interface**\n   - Routes exchanges between processors\n   - Manages interceptor strategies\n   - Manages error handler attachment\n   - Initializes and post-initializes processor chains\n\n7. **Pipeline**\n   - Chains processors sequentially\n   - Manages async execution\n   - Handles exchange copying between processors\n   - Uses PooledExchangeTask pattern for efficiency\n\n8. **RouteReifier**\n   - Converts RouteDefinition to Route\n   - Resolves input endpoints\n   - Orchestrates route creation\n   - Applies route-level policies and advice\n\n9. **ProcessorReifier**\n   - Converts individual ProcessorDefinitions to Processors\n   - Wraps processors in Channels\n   - Applies processor-level error handling\n   - Manages interceptor strategies at processor level\n\n### Data Flow Description\n\n```\nMessage Reception to Delivery:\n1. Endpoint receives external message\n2. Consumer.createExchange(true) creates Exchange wrapper\n3. Consumer calls Processor.process(exchange)\n   - Processor is the route's entry Channel\n\n4. Route entry Channel (with UnitOfWork advice):\n   - Starts UnitOfWork transaction scope\n   - Invokes RoutePipeline\n\n5. RoutePipeline chains all route processors:\n   - For each processor P in pipeline:\n     a. Prepare exchange (OUT\u2192IN copy if needed)\n     b. Get next Processor in pipeline\n     c. Check continueProcessing() conditions\n     d. Call P.process(exchange, callback)\n\n6. Each processor (e.g., To definition):\n   - May wrapped in Channel with interceptors:\n     a. Apply InterceptStrategy wrappers (debugger, tracer, etc.)\n     b. Apply error handler\n\n7. Producer invokes send:\n   - Invokes Producer.process(exchange)\n   - Producer implementation sends to external endpoint\n\n8. Response handling (for request-reply):\n   - Response wrapped in new Exchange\n   - Returned to Consumer\n\n9. Consumer calls UnitOfWork.done():\n   - Finalizes transaction\n   - Releases Exchange resources (if autoRelease=true)\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n1. **Component \u2192 Endpoint Contract**\n   - Component creates Endpoint instance\n   - Endpoint lifecycle managed by CamelContext\n   - Component may configure Endpoint after creation\n\n2. **Endpoint \u2192 Consumer/Producer Contract**\n   - Endpoint creates Consumer with Processor callback\n   - Consumer invokes Processor to route consumed messages\n   - Endpoint creates Producer for outbound routing\n   - Producer extends Processor (polymorphic)\n\n3. **Producer/Consumer \u2192 Processor Contract**\n   - Both implement Processor interface\n   - Same signature: `process(Exchange exchange)`\n   - Allows transparent composition in pipelines\n\n4. **Processor \u2192 Channel Contract**\n   - Processor wrapped in Channel\n   - Channel acts as transparent decorator\n   - Channel adds interceptor/error handling behavior\n   - Next processor accessed via Channel.getNextProcessor()\n\n5. **Channel \u2192 InterceptStrategy Contract**\n   - Channel delegates to InterceptStrategy.wrapProcessorInInterceptors()\n   - Interceptor returns wrapped Processor\n   - Interceptor must return AsyncProcessor\n   - Multiple interceptors chain decoratively\n\n6. **Route \u2192 ProcessorReifier Contract**\n   - ProcessorReifier.addRoutes() adds Channel to route\n   - Route.getEventDrivenProcessors() collects all channels\n   - RoutePipeline chains all event-driven processors\n   - InternalProcessor wraps entire pipeline with advice\n\n## Summary\n\nApache Camel's message routing architecture implements a sophisticated **Component\u2192Endpoint\u2192Consumer/Producer\u2192Processor** hierarchy bridged by the **Reifier pattern**. Messages flow from external endpoints through event-driven consumers into a **Pipeline of Channels**, where each channel wraps processors with **interceptor strategies** and **error handlers** using an **Advice pattern**. The **RouteReifier** and **ProcessorReifier** classes form a model-to-runtime bridge that transforms declarative **ProcessorDefinitions** (DSL) into executable **Processors**, applying cross-cutting concerns (debugging, tracing, management) through **CamelInternalProcessorAdvice** instances. This architecture achieves separation of concerns between modeling (camel-core-model), compilation (camel-core-reifier), execution (camel-core-processor), and interception (camel-base-engine), enabling flexible EIP-based routing with extensible lifecycle management and debugging capabilities.\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/solution.md
# Apache Camel Message Routing Architecture Analysis

## Files Examined

### Core API Layer (camel-api)
- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Component.java** — Factory interface for creating Endpoint instances; defines `createEndpoint(String uri)` as the entry point for endpoint creation
- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Endpoint.java** — Message endpoint interface implementing the Message Endpoint pattern; methods include `createProducer()`, `createConsumer(Processor)`, `createExchange()`
- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Producer.java** — Sends message exchanges to an endpoint; implements Processor interface
- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Consumer.java** — Consumes message exchanges from an endpoint; contains `getProcessor()` for message processing
- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Processor.java** — Core unit for message processing; single method `process(Exchange exchange)`
- **core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Channel.java** — Intercept channel between processors in route graph; methods include `initChannel()` and `postInitChannel()` for interceptor wiring

### Base Engine Layer (camel-base-engine)
- **core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultChannel.java** — Default Channel implementation; wraps processors with interceptors, error handlers, and debugging/tracing advice via `initChannel()` method (lines 148-271)
- **core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/CamelInternalProcessor.java** — Base class for DefaultChannel; manages internal processor advices for management and lifecycle
